686	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Badol Sarker Vs. Jaynal Khan and others, (Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 1215 of 2016  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Mostafizur Rahman, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Badol Sarker </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Jaynal Khan and another </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REIVSIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 178px; margin-right: auto;" width="647"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 289.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__November__18(2)/Issue%20__November__18(2)__C.%20R.%201215%20of%2016__Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Chowdhury,%20J__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Badol Sarker</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Defendant-Appellant-Petitioner</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Jaynal Khan and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Plaintiff-Respondent-Opposite parties</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Order XXVI, Rule 9</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Advocate Commissioner’s Report was given after a field survey and an appropriate measurement of land becomes binding upon a party, even, any inconvenience is caused because the report has been accepted by passing a final decree in this partition suit. In this regard my observation is that if the parties could not reach to an amicable partition then the partition by a court proceeding must be accepted. ...(13 and 14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> Mostafizur Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Shasti Sarker, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J.</span></u></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> At the</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> instance of the present-defendant-appellant-petitioner, Badol Sarker, this Rule has been issued calling upon the opposite-party Nos.1-5 to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and decree dated 14.03.2016 passed by the learned District Judge, Manikganj in Title Appeal No.14 of 2015 affirming those date 28.08.2014 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Harirampur, Manikganj in Partition Suit No.10 of 2000 should not be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The relevant facts for disposal of this Rule, <em>inter-alia,</em> are that the present-opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed the Title Suit No.10 of 2000 in the court of the learned Assistant Judge, Manikganj for partition of the suit described in the plaint. The case of the plaint, is that, the suit land was originally belonged to C.S. recorded tenant Kantu Pramanik, Nargarbasi, Dhanmani and Hriday Pramanik in course of inheritance and transfer by way of sale deed and heba-bill-ewaj one Hossain Ali became the owner of 90 decimals of land, who transferred the land to his son Hafizuddin Biswas on 24.02.1964 by a deed of heba-bil-ewaj, who again sold 20 decimals of land to the present-plaintiff-opposite parties thereby the plaintiffs became the owner of 19 decimals of land in Dag No.303 and 1 decimal of land in Dag No.305 but when the plaintiffs claimed for partition the defendant denied.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The present-petitioner as the defendant contested the suit by filing a written statement denying the statement of the plaint in the suit along with others. The suit was originally owned by Raj Krishna and Baru Pramanik but the C.S. record was prepared only in the name of Raj Krishna, even though, he was enjoying only ½ decimal of land and he died leaving behind a son Lusmon who died leaving behind Hriday Pramanimk and wife Nanda Rani as the legal heirs in course of inheritance and the suit land was sold to one Hossain Ali on 02.07.1934 from Dag No.424, 145, 303 and 305 but the S.A. record was wrongly published for the land measuring 1.06 acres<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in different Dags, particularly, 10 decimals of land in Dag No.305 and 25 decimals of land in Dag No.303 and R.S. record was also published in the name of Hafizuddin Biswas, son of Hossain Ali, who claimed that his father purchased 37 decimals of land in Plot No.303. The defendant claimed that he was the owner of the land measuring 3.33½ acres of land but he was in possession of total land measuring 2.35 acres of land as the heir of Kokaram Pramanik.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">After hearing the parties the learned trial court decreed the suit in preliminary form by his judgment and decree dated 16.08.2001. After the preliminary decree the Title Appeal No.73 of 2005 was filed to the learned appellate court, who remanded the suit to the trial court. However, a Civil Revision No.2212 of 2006 was filed in this Court which was discharged on 24.01.2010 in order to get a fresh Advocate Commissioner Report for making the decree final. On 06.021.2011 an Advocate Commissioner was appointed who submitted a report allocating saham of the present-plaintiff-opposite parties upon the land measuring 6 decimals from Dag No.303 and 14 decimals of land in Dag No.305 and the present-defendant-petitioner No.1 along with other defendants got saham of .20 acres accordingly, the final decree was passed on 28.08.2014. Being aggrieved by the said final decree the present-petitioner preferred the Title Appeal No.14 of 2015 which was heard and dismissed on 14.03.2016 by the impugned judgment and decree. This revisional application has been filed under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure challenging the legality of the said impugned judgment and decree passed by the learned appellate court and the present Rule was issued thereupon.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Md. Mostafizur Rahman, the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner submits that both the courts below misread, non considered about the saham allotted to defendant No.1 on the basis of wrong report of Advocate Commissioner, as such, committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice and the same is liable to be set aside.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">     </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate further submits that the courts below did not consider the defendant No.1 has constructed his residence in 80 decimals of land in Plot No.303 and the written objection upon the said Advocate Commissioner’s Report and thus, it has committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision, and the said decree is liable to be set aside.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Rule has been opposed by the present-opposite party No.1-5.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Shahsti Sarker, the learned Advocate appearing for the opposite parties submits that the preliminary decree was passed on 16.08.2001 after considering the appropriate measurement of 20 decimals of land in favour of the plaintiffs from Dag Nos.303 and 305, however, after the fresh Advocate Commissioner’s Report on remand of the suit the plaintiffs were given 6 decimals of land in Dag No.303 and 14 decimals of land in Dag No. 305 and the plaintiffs could prove their entitlement upon the said measurement of land in all the courts below through the Exhibits-1-5, as such, the courts below committed no error of law by a concurrent judgment in favour of the plaintiffs but the present-petitioner obtained the instant Rule by misleading the court, therefore, the Rule is liable to be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate further submits that the Advocate Commissioner’s Report was accepted by the learned trial court before making the decree final and after examining all the relevant documents, therefore, no interference from this Court is called for.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Considering the above submissions made by the learned Advocates appearing of the respective parties and also considering the revisional application filed under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure along with Annexures therein, in particular, the impugned judgment and decree passed by the appellate court and also considering the materials in the lower court records, it appears to me that the present-opposite parties as the plaintiffs filed a title suit for a partition upon the land measuring 20 decimals of land in Dag Nos.303 and 305, appertaining to Khatian No.53, Mouja East Khalilpur, Police Station Harirampur, District-Manikganj. In support of the plaintiffs’ case Exhibit-1 was submitted as the record of right, Exhibit-2 was the deed dated 02.07.1934 and also a record of the earlier Title Suit No.144 of 1932 among others.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On the other hand, the defendant had submitted as Exhibits-Ka and Chcha’ in support of his claim of land measuring 2.35 acres. After examining the above Exhibits the learned trial court passed the preliminary decree in preliminary form for the land measuring 20 decimals of land out of which 19 decimals of land from Dag No.303 and 1 decimal of land from Dag No.305. However, the said decree was made final by the trial court after a lengthy process of litigation between/among the parties and in the final decree the present-opposite parties as the plaintiffs got 20 decimals of land out of which<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>6 decimals of land from Dag No.303 and 14 decimals of land from Dag No.305. The present-petitioner as the defendant No.1 got saham 2.1075 acres of land under the final decree<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as per the learned Advocate Commissioner’s Report submitted in the trial court pursuant to the order of this Court upon a revisional application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">I have considered the final decree and the exhibits for entitlement of the parties and I found that the trial court and the learned appellate court have properly read and understood by considering those documents, particularly, the Advocate Commissioner’s Report finally submitted on 12.04.2011, therefore, I consider that the courts below committed no error of law by allocating saham of 20 decimals of land<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>for the plaintiff-opposite parties and the saham of 2.1075 acres of land in favour of the present-petitioner.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate for the petitioner drawn an attention of this Court that the land and final Advocate Commissioner’s Report caused serious difficulty as the home land has been taken away from the petitioner by the final decree. In this regard, I consider that the Advocate Commissioner’s Report was given after a field survey and an appropriate measurement of land becomes binding upon a party, even, any inconvenience is caused because the report has been accepted by passing a final decree in this partition suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In this regard my observation is that if the parties not could reached to an amicable partition then the partition by a court proceeding must be accepted.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">I am now inclined to examine the judgment and decree passed by the learned courts below. The learned trial court came to a lawful conclusion by passing the final decree on 28.08.2014 on the basis of the following finding:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 31.5pt; line-height: 115%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; line-height: 112%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Accordingly, I do not find merit in the Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the result, the Rule is discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The ad-interim order of stay granted at the time of issuance of the Rule upon proceedings in Execution Case No.3 of 2015 pending in the court learned Assistant Judge, Harrirampur, Manikganj is hereby recalled and vacated. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The office is directed to communicate this judgment and order to the concerned court immediately and the office is also directed to send down the lower courts’ record at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__November__18(2)/Issue%20__November__18(2)__C.%20R.%201215%20of%2016__Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Chowdhury,%20J__5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">1215 of 2016</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
687	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bangladesh and others Vs. Professor Nurul Islam &amp; another, (Syed Mahmud Hossain, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APEAL Nos. 204-205 of 2001  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Surendra Kumar Sonha, CJ.  Syed Mahmud Hossain, J Hasan Foez Siddique, J Mirza Hussain Haider, J.  Mohammad Bazlur Rahman, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Ekramul Haque, Deputy Attorney General, instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)     </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Professor Nurul Islam, Al-haj Nur Mohammad</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitution of Bangladesh, </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Surendra Kumar Sonha, CJ. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">01.03.2016</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 12.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="16"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__November__18(2)/Issue__NOVEMBER_%2018(2)__C.%20A.%20204-205%20of%2001__Syed%20Mahmud%20Hossain,%20J__AD___3_.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 106.55pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" width="142"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Government of Bangladesh and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Appellants</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In all the appeals)</span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Professor Nurul Islam</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . Respondent</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C.A. No.204/01)</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Al-haj Nur Mohammad</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Respondent.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(In C.A. No.205/01)</span></em></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"> Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="color: #000000;">Articles 21, 31 and 32</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">The inalienable right of every citizen, wherever</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> he may be, and of every other person for the time being within Bangladesh, and in particular no action detrimental to the life, liberty, body, reputation or property of any person shall be taken except in accordance with law. According to Article 32 no person shall be deprived of life or personal liberty save in accordance with law. Therefore, right to life is a fundamental right subject to law of the land. In the absence of any interpretation of right to life in our jurisdiction we have to see what meaning was given by the superior Courts of other countries to right to life. Right to life is not only limited to protection of life and limbs but also extends to the protection of health, enjoyment of pollution free water and air, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">bare necessaries of life, facilities for education,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> maternity benefit, maintenance and improvement of public health by creating and sustaining conditions congenial to good health and ensuring quality of life consistent to human dignity. . . . (45 and 52)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Articles 18(1), 31 and 32</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The State shall regard the rising of level of nutrition and the improvement of public health as among its primary duties, and in particular shall adopt effective measures to prevent the consumption, except for medical purposes or for such other purposes as may be prescribed by law, of alcohol and other intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious to health. Though the aforesaid provision cannot be enforced by the Court it can be seen for interpreting the meaning of right of life under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution. A man has natural right to enjoyment of healthy life and longevity up to normal expectation of life of an ordinary human being. Enjoyment of healthy life and </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">normal expectation of longevity is threatened</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> by diseases, natural calamities and human actions. When a person is grievously hurt or injured by another his life and longevity are threatened. Similarly when a man smokes which is injurious to his health he suffers ailments and his life and normal expectation of longevity are threatened. It is the natural right of a man to live free from all man-made hazards of life and such right has been guaranteed under the aforesaid Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution subject to law of the land. No one has any right to endanger the life of the people which includes their health and normal longevity of an ordinary healthy person. Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution not only means protection of life and limbs necessary for full enjoyment of life but also includes amongst others protection of health and normal longevity of an ordinary human being. It is the obligation of the State to discourage smoking and consumption of tobacco materials and the improvement of public health by preventing advertisement of tobacco made products. Though the obligation under Article 18(1) of the Constitution cannot be enforced, State is bound to protect the health and longevity of the people living in the country as right to life guaranteed under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution includes protection of health and longevity of a man free from threats of man-made hazards. Right to life under the aforesaid Articles of the Constitution being fundamental right it can be enforced by this Court to remove any unjustified threat to health and longevity of the people as the same are included in the right to life.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (54)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Tobacco Product Usage Control Act (XI of 2005)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 4</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The provisions of this Act and the Rules made thereunder are not being properly implemented particularly as regards prohibition of smoking in public places and selling of tobacco products to minors. We have also noticed that in public places, the facilities relating to smoking such as ashtrays, matches, lighters are kept. It has become necessary to save our posterity from the curse of tobacco addiction and to inform them about the Smoking and Tobacco Product Usage Control Act, 2005 as amended by the Smoking and Tobacco Usage (Control) Amended Act, 2013 and also the Rules made thereunder. Therefore, we are inclined to give four more directives in addition to the directives given by the High Court Division.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">I. The law enforcing agencies are directed to implement the provision of section 4 of the Act, which provides that no person shall smoke in any public place and public transport and that if any person smokes in contravention of sub-section (1) shall be punishable with fine not exceeding three hundred </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">taka and the penalty shall be doubled</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> for each subsequent violation.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">II. The law enforcing agencies are directed to ensure that no one can sell tobacco product to a minor as per sub-section (1) of section 6(a) and sub-section (2) thereof provided if any person contravenes the provision of sub-section (1) he shall be punishable with fine which may extend to five thousand taka and if a person contravenes the provisions more than once, every time the amount of fine shall be doubled.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">III. The owner, proprietor of a </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">public </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">place shall ensure that no person</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> smokes</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> in that place. Ashtrays, matches, lighters and other things designed to facilitate smoking are not to be provided in public place where smoking is prohibited altogether. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">IV. The Ministry of Education, the Ministry of Primary and Mass </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Education and the National Curriculum</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Textbook Board (NCTB) are directed</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> to incorporate a chapter in the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">curriculum of schools and intermediate</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> colleges about the adverse effect of smoking and also about the latest law in this regard.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . .(68)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Dr. Mohiuddin Farooque Vs. Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Commerce, Government of the People’s </span></em></strong><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Republic of Bangladesh, Bangladesh Secretariat</span></em></strong><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> and others, 48 DLR 438; Munn Vs. Illinois (1877) 94 US 113; Francis Coralie Vs. Union Territory of Delhi, AIR 1981 SC 746; Bandhua Mukti Morcha Vs. Union of India, AIR 1984 SC 802; Vincent Vs. Union of India AIR 1987 SC 990; Vikram Deo Singh Vs. State of Bihar, AIR 1988 SC 1782; Subash Kumar Vs. the State of Bihar, AIR 1991 SC 420 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Appellants,</span></b><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'> </span><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>(In all theappeals)</span><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>)</span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">: Mr. Ekramul </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Haque, Deputy Attorney General,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Respondents,</span></b><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'></span><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>(In all the appeals)</span><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Ex-parte</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Both the appeals, by leave, are directed against the judgment and order dated 07.02.2000 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos. 1825 and 4521 of 1999 making the Rules absolute with direction. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Both the appeals involving similar questions of laws and facts having been heard together are now disposed of by this single judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The facts, leading to the filing of these civil appeals, in a nutshell, are:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 22.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Professor Nurul Islam is a National Professor and the President of ‘ADHUNIK’ (Amara Dhumpan Nibaran Kori),which is registered under Voluntary Social Welfare Organization Registration &amp; Control Ordinance,1961, working and lobbying for anti-smoking causes. The writ-petitioner obtained Rule from the High Court Division as to why section 3 of the ‘Tamakjato Shamogri Biponon Niontrener Jonno Pronito Ain 1988’ </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(ZvgvKRvZ mvgMÖx wecYY wbqš¿‡bi Rb¨ cªbxZ AvBb, 1988)</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> should not be enforced properly and why should not be directed to enact, in the light of <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the Ordinance No.16 of 1990, for the prohibition</span> of all forms of tobacco advertisement.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The case of the writ-petitioner is that section 3(1) of ‘Tamakjatio Shamogri Biponon Niontrener Jonno Pronito Ain’ provides for a statutory warning that the smoking is dangerous for health and the warning must be printed on packet or canned tobacco based products on a prominent and distinct space of the container of the packet, which would be easily readable and understood. Similarly, section 3(2) of the said Act states that no advertisement of tobacco based products shall be published, broadcast or displayed without having the said warning in easily readable and understood Bengali engraved, written or printed on a prominent part of the advertisement. In breach of section 3(1) of the statute, the companies engaged in tobacco business are printing the statutory warning in obscure corners of tobacco packets and containers and publish the warning in such small size that it is barely readable. In advertisements with moving images in the movie theatres and those broadcast on television the statutory warnings are shown so briefly and without any voice that they have little or no effect on the viewers.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">It is accepted not only by the medical researchers but also by tobacco industries in developed countries that tobacco consumption leads to fatal diseases such as cancer, lung and heart diseases causing about 3.5 million deaths each year and one million of deaths occur in developing countries like Bangladesh. Global tobacco epidemic is predicted to claim premature death of some 250 million children and adolescents at present, a third of these shall occur in developing countries. By 2020 it is predicted that the tobacco will become the leading death and disability, killing more than 10 million people annually. The writ-petitioner further stated that the passive smoking also has dangerous effect on health. It was accepted that great majority of rural people in Bangladesh, who consume tobacco based products are illiterate and completely unaware of the dangers and the harm of consuming them. Even if, the statutory warning is written on a distinct space of the packets, it would not make any sense to the illiterate consumers. Considering the dangers of consuming tobacco products, mere enforcement of section 3 of the Act,1988 would be useless unless the manufacturing, consumption and promotion of tobacco related products are prohibited. Although smoking is in decline in the industrialized world the consumption of cigarettes rose by 67% in developing countries between 1970 and 1994 and tobacco related deaths in developing countries will rise from one million in a year to seven million in a year by 2030. A similar Writ Petition No. 4521 of 1999 was filed by Al-haj Nur Mohammad against manufacture, sale and advertisement of tobacco products.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The writ-respondents entered appearance to oppose the Rules and made submissions to controvert the materials on record made in the writ petitions. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The learned Judges of the High Court Division upon hearing the parties by the judgment and order dated 07.02.2000 made the Rules absolute with direction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with judgment and order passed by the High Court Division, the writ-respondents as the leave petitioners have filed Civil Petitions for Leave to Appeal Nos.670 and 667 of 2000 before this Division and obtained leave in both the civil petitions on 29.03.2001, resulting in Civil Appeal Nos.204 and 2005 of 2001.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mr. Ekramul Haque, learned Deputy Attorney General, appearing on behalf of the appellants of both the civil appeals, submits that the High Court Division in exercise of its jurisdiction under Article 102 of the Constitution cannot direct the legislature to pass any law unless there has been positive violations of the Constitution and there is a necessity to rectify the wrong and that Parliament having not passed any law in violation of any provision of the Constitution cannot be directed to pass any law in a specified field and that the High Court Division is indirectly requiring the Parliament to pass any law by giving direction to the Government and as such, the impugned judgment should be set aside. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">None appeared on behalf of the respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Deputy Attorney General, perused the impugned judgment and the materials on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Before entering into the merit of the appeals, it would be pertinent to go through the grounds, for which, leave was granted in both the appeals. The grounds are quoted below:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(i) For that in the absence of any law in derogation of the fundamental rights ensured by the Constitution for the rectification of which the Court can give direction, the High Court Division was in error of law in giving direction compliance of which necessitates legislation and thus indirectly requiring Parliament to pass laws.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(ii) For that the High Court Division was in error in not taking into consideration that Parliament has not passed any law which is in derogation of the right to life and Parliament which has plenary jurisdiction to decide what law to be passed and as such the High Court Division cannot give direction to the Government to do things which will require backing of law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iii) For that the learned judges of the High Court Division has been grossly in error of law in relying too liberally on the Principles of State Policy incorporated in Articles 11 and 18 of the Constitution without appreciating that such principles are not to be enforced in disregard of the social realities and that they are not to be judicially enforced.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iv) For that the High Court Division has failed to appreciate that under the constitutional dispensation, the legislature should remain left with the task of looking after the questions involved in the matter and in that view, it has acted in disregard of the intent and purport of Article 47(1)(f) of the Constitution. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(v) For that in consideration of the existing laws on the subject in question and the policies and principles enshrined in the Constitution, it is the legislature that should be left to the job of looking for the occasion to bring in necessary ban and/or restriction to meet the problem.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The High Court Division observed that the Fundamental State Policy enshrined particularly in Articles 11 and 14 of the Constitution shall be a guide to the interpretation of the Constitution and the laws of the country to enforce fundamental rights of citizens. The High Court Division found that the effect of advertisement of tobacco based products is definitely designed to the detriment of right to life of the citizens, particularly the younger generation which is guaranteed by Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution and they are entitled to protection of law from being exposed to the hazards of cigarette smoking through advertisements. The High Court Division observed that in view of the fundamental state policy enshrined in Article 18 providing for raising of the level of nutrition and the improvement of quality of public health, as its primary duties, and in particular shall adopt effective measures to prevent consumption of alcoholic and other intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious to health and the provision in Article 11 providing for the dignity and worth of human person which although are not judicially enforceable they are the inviolable fundamental principles of state policy and shall he applied by the State in the making of laws and shall guide the interpretation of the Constitution and the laws of the country. The High Court Division therefore held that the writ-respondents and the authorities performing the functions in connection with the affairs of the Republic that advertisement in any form of Cigarette, Bidi, tobacco related products must not be continued in any manner in Newspapers, Magazines, Signboards or in any electronic medias like Television/Radio beyond the period of the existing contract/agreement with the manufacturers or their agents. The said authorities were duty bound to see that any other authority, private or public does not flout the direction in any manner. The High Court Division made the following specific directions:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">a) The government shall take steps phase by phase to stop production of tobacco leaves in tobacco growing Districts of Bangladesh, giving subsidy to the farmers, if possible and necessary to produce other agricultural products instead of tobacco and for rehabilitation of the tobacco workers engaged in tobacco production, if possible with alternative beneficial jobs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">b) The Government shall restrict issuance of license for setting up tobacco industry or Bidi factory and direct the existing tobacco and Bidi Companies to switch over to some other industry to prevent production of Cigarette, Bidi and other tobacco related products, specifying a reasonable period for the purpose. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">c) To prohibit importation of Cigarette or tobacco related product within a reasonable period and meanwhile to impose heavy tax for the import and to print the statutory warning legibly in bold words in Bengali.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">d) The Government, the concerned Ministry of the Broadcasting Television Authority, Newspaper of Bill-Board authority or any other agencies engaged in advertisement shall not advertise or telecast any cigarette/bidi related advertisement or commercials and shall not undertake any show/program/propagating cigarette/bidi smoking among the citizens. This direction shall be effective/after the expiry of the existing contract of advertisement between them and the manufactures or their agents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">e) The Government and/or any concerned authority shall not undertake or encourage any promotional ventures like “Voyage or Discovery” and those shall be strictly prohibited.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The Government shall direct the appropriate authorities to take steps prohibiting smoking in public and public places like Train, Railway Station, Bus, and Station, Ferry- Ghat, Steamer in any public gathering/meeting/ assembly making the atmosphere noxious to health taking resort to strict complacence with the existing provisions of Sections 278, 133, 188, of the Penal Code.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Leading cause of death, illness and impoverishment</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The tobacco epidemic is one of the biggest public health threats the world has ever faced, killing around 6 million people a year. More than 5 million of those deaths are the result of direct tobacco use while more than 600000 are the result of non-smokers being exposed to second-hand smoke.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Nearly 80% of the more than 1 billion smokers worldwide live in low- and middleincome countries, where the burden of tobacco-related illness and death is heaviest. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Tobacco users who die prematurely deprive</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> their families of income, raise the cost of health care and hinder economic development. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In some countries, children from poor households are frequently employed in tobacco farming to provide family income. These children are especially vulnerable to "green tobacco sickness", which is caused by the nicotine that is absorbed through the skin from the handling of wet tobacco leaves.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Surveillance is key</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Good monitoring tracks the extent and character of the tobacco epidemic and indicates how best to tailor policies. Only 1 in 3 countries, representing one third of the world's population, monitors tobacco use by repeating nationally representative youth and adult surveys at least once every 5 years.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Second-hand smoke kills</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Second-hand smoke is the smoke that fills restaurants, offices or other enclosed spaces when people burn tobacco products such as cigarettes, <em>bidis </em>and water-pipes. There are more than 4000 chemicals in tobacco smoke, of which at least 250 are known to be harmful and more than 50 are known to cause cancer.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">There is no safe level of exposure to second-hand tobacco smoke</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> In adults, second-hand smoke causes serious cardiovascular and <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">respiratory diseases, including coronary</span> heart disease and lung cancer. In infants, it causes sudden death. In pregnant women, it causes low birth weight.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Almost half of children regularly breathe air polluted by tobacco smoke in public places.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 40.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Second-hand smoke causes more than 600 000 premature deaths per year.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 40.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> In 2004, children accounted for 28% of the deaths attributable to second-hand smoke.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Every person should be able to breathe tobacco-smoke-free air. Smoke-free laws protect the health of non-smokers, are popular, do not harm business and encourage smokers to quit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
