mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Over 1.3 billion people, or 18% of the world's population, are protected by comprehensive national smoke-free laws.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Tobacco users need help to quit</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Studies show that few people understand the specific health risks of tobacco use.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Among smokers who are aware of the dangers of tobacco, most want to quit. Counselling and medication can more than double the chance that a smoker who tries to quit will succeed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">National comprehensive cessation services</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> with full or partial cost-coverage are available to assist tobacco users to quit in only 24 countries, representing 15% of the world's population.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">There is no cessation assistance of any kind in one quarter of low-income countries.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Picture warnings work </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Hard-hitting anti-tobacco advertisements</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> and graphic pack warnings – especially those that include pictures – reduce the number of children who begin smoking and increase the number of smokers who quit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Graphic warnings can persuade smokers to protect the health of non-smokers by smoking less inside the home and avoiding smoking near children. Studies carried out after the implementation of pictorial package warnings in Brazil, Canada, Singapore and Thailand consistently show that pictorial warnings significantly increase people's awareness of the harms of tobacco use. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Only 42 countries, representing 19% of the world's population, meet the best practice for pictorial warnings, which includes the warnings in the local language and cover an average of at least half of the front and back of cigarette packs. Most of these countries are low- or middle-income countries.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mass media campaigns can also reduce tobacco consumption by influencing people to protect non-smokers and convincing youths to stop using tobacco.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Over half of the world's population live in the 39 countries that have aired at least 1 strong anti-tobacco mass media campaign within the last 2 years.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bans on tobacco advertising, promotion and sponsorship can reduce tobacco consumption.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> A comprehensive ban on all tobacco advertising, promotion and sponsorship could decrease tobacco consumption by an average of about 7%, with some countries experiencing a decline in consumption of up to 16%.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Only 29 countries, representing 12% of the world’s population, have completely banned all forms of tobacco advertising, promotion and sponsorship.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Around 1 country in 3 has minimal or no restrictions at all on tobacco advertising, promotion and sponsorship.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Taxes discourage tobacco use</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Tobacco taxes are the most cost-effective way to reduce tobacco use, especially among young and poor people. A tax increase that increases tobacco prices by 10% decreases tobacco consumption by about 4% in high-income countries and about 5% in low- and middle-income countries.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Even so, high tobacco taxes is a measure that is rarely implemented. Only 33 countries, with 10% of the world's population, have introduced taxes on tobacco products so that more than 75% of the retail price is tax. Tobacco tax revenues are on average 269 times higher than spending on tobacco control, based on available data.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Illicit trade of tobacco products must be stopped</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The illicit trade in tobacco products poses major health, economic and security concerns around the world. It is estimated that 1 in every 10 cigarettes and tobacco products consumed globally is illicit. The illicit market is supported by various players, ranging from petty peddlers to organized criminal networks involved in arms and human trafficking. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Eliminating illicit trade in tobacco will reduce the harmful consumption of tobacco by restricting availability of cheap, unregulated alternatives and increasing overall tobacco prices. Critically, this will reduce premature deaths from tobacco use and raise tax revenue for governments. Stopping illicit trade in tobacco products is a health priority, and is achievable. But to do so requires improvement of national and sub-national tax administration systems and international collaboration, such as ratification and implementation of the Protocol to Eliminate the Illicit Trade in Tobacco Products, an international treaty in its own right, negotiated by parties to the WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control (WHO FCTC).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">While publicly stating its support for action against the illicit trade, the tobacco industry’s behind-the-scenes behaviour has been very different. Internal industry documents released as a result of court cases demonstrate that the tobacco industry has actively fostered the illicit trade globally. It also works to block implementation of tobacco control measures, such as tax increases and pictorial health warnings, by misleadingly arguing they will fuel the illicit trade.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">WHO response</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control entered into force in February 2005. Since then, it has become one of the most widely embraced treaties in the history of the United Nations with 180 Parties covering 90% of the world's population.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The WHO Framework Convention is WHO's most important tobacco control tool and a milestone in the promotion of public health. It is an evidence-based treaty that reaffirms the right of people to the highest standard of health, provides legal dimensions for international health cooperation and sets high standards for compliance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In 2008, WHO introduced a practical, cost-effective way to scale up implementation of provisions of the WHO Framework Convention on the ground: MPOWER. Each MPOWER measure corresponds to at least 1 provision of the WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The 6 MPOWER measures are:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Monitor tobacco use and prevention policies</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Protect people from tobacco use</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Offer help to quit tobacco use</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Warn about the dangers of tobacco</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Enforce bans on tobacco advertising, promotion and sponsorship</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'MS Mincho'; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'MS Mincho';"></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Raise taxes on tobacco.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The WHO FCTC Protocol to Eliminate the Illicit Trade in Tobacco Products requires a wide range of measures relating to the tobacco supply chain, including the licensing of imports, exports and manufacture of tobacco products; the establishment of tracking and tracing systems and the imposition of penal sanctions on those responsible for illicit trade. It would also criminalize illicit production and cross-border smuggling. <strong>(extracted from WHO Website)</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Though the case of <strong><em>Dr. Mohiuddin Farooque Vs. Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Commerce, Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh, Bangladesh Secretariat and others, 48 DLR 438 </em></strong>is different from the case in hand, the principle expounded in that case may be taken into consideration in respect of the case in hand. In the aforesaid reported case, respondent No.6 Danish Condensed Milk Bangladesh Limited imported 500 metric tons of skimmed milk powder from Holland. Upon clearance of the consignment radiation test was made and found 133 Bq radiation per kilogram which was above the minimum approved radiation level of 95 Bq and was opined that the consignment in question should not be marketed. Therefore, Secretary General of Bangladesh Environmental Lawyers’ Association (BELA) filed a writ petition in public interest as consumption of imported food item containing radiation level above the acceptable limit is injurious to public health. Therefore, the writ petitioner prayed that the respondents be directed to take measure for sending back the said milk powder to the exporter. The High Court Division on the fact of the said case held as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“It is the primary obligation of the State to raise the level of nutrition and the improvement of public health by preventing use of contaminated food, drink, etc. Though that obligation under Article 18(1) of the Constitution cannot be enforced state is bound to protect the health and longevity of the people living in the country as right to life guaranteed under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution includes protection of health and normal longevity of a man free from threats of man-made hazards unless that threat is justified by law. Right to life under the aforesaid Articles of the Constitution being a fundamental right it can be enforced by this Court to remove any unjustified threat to the health and longevity of the people as the same are included in the right to life.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">45.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">According to Article 31 of the Constitution, to enjoy the protection of the law, and to be treated in accordance with law, is the inalienable right of every citizen, wherever he may be, and of every other person for the time being within Bangladesh, and in particular no action detrimental to the life, liberty, body, reputation or property of any person shall be taken except in accordance with law. According to Article 32 no person shall be deprived of life or personal liberty save in accordance with law. Therefore, right to life is a fundamental right subject to law of the land. In the absence of any interpretation of right to life in our jurisdiction we have to see what meaning was given by the superior Courts of other countries to right to life. Fifth Amendment to the Constitution of the United States of America declares: “No person shall be deprived of his life, liberty or property without due process of law. Fourteen Amendment also imposes similar limitation on the state. In the case of <strong><em>Munn Vs. Illinois (1877) 94 US 113 </em></strong>in his dissenting judgment <strong>Field J: </strong>interpreted “life” under the aforesaid provisions of the US Constitution as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Something more than mere animal existence. The inhibition against its deprivation extends to all those limbs and faculties by which life is enjoyed. The provision equally prohibits the mutilation of the body by the amputation of an arm or leg or the putting out of any eye, or the destruction of any other organ of the body through which the soul communicates with the outer world.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">46.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">According to Article 21 of the Indian Constitution: “No person shall be deprived of life or personal liberty except according to procedure established by law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">47.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Indian Supreme Court interpreted the right to life under the aforesaid Article 21 of the Indian Constitution similar to our Article 32 in several cases. The cases of <strong><em>Francis</em></strong><strong><em> Coralie V. Union Territory of Delhi reported in AIR 1981 SC 746, </em></strong>right to life under Article 21 of the Indian Constitution has been interpreted in the following words:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“But the question which arises is whether the right to life is limited only to protection of limb or faculty or does it go further and embrace something more. We think that the right to life includes the right to life with human dignity and all that goes along with it, namely, the bare necessaries of life such as adequate nutrition, clothing and shelter over the head and facilities for reading, writing and expressing oneself in diverse forms, freely moving about and mixing and commingling with fellow human beings.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">48.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of <strong><em>Bandhua Mukti Morcha V. Union of India reported in AIR 1984 SC 802</em></strong>, Supreme Court of India while interpreting Article 21 of the Indian Constitution further extended the meaning of right to life as made in the earlier case in the following words:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“....It must include protection of the health and strength of workers, men and women, and of the tender age of children against abuse, opportunities and facilities for children to develop in a healthy manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity, educational facilities, just and humane conditions of work and maternity relief.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">49.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of <strong><em>Vincent V. Union of India reported in AIR 1987 SC 990 </em></strong>learned Judge delivering the judgment in that case quoted with approval interpretation of right to life made by the Indian Supreme Court in the <strong>Bandhua Mukti Morcha </strong>case held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“A healthy body is the very foundation for all human activities. ...............In a welfare state, therefore, it is the obligation of the State to ensure the creation and the sustaining of conditions congenial to good health...... Maintenance and improvement of public health have a rank high as these are indispensable to the very physical existence of the community and on the betterment of these depends the building of the society of which the Constitution markers envisaged.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">50.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of <strong><em>Vikram</em></strong><strong><em> Deo Singh V. State of Bihar reported in AIR 1988 SC 1782 </em></strong>it was further held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“We live in an age when this Court has demonstrated, while interpreting Article 21 of the Constitution, that every person is entitled to quality of life consistent with his human personality. The right to life with human dignity is the fundamental right of every Indian citizen.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">51.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In the case of <strong><em>Subash Kumar Vs. the State of Bihar reported in AIR 1991 SC 420 </em></strong>it was further held:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“Right to live is a fundamental right under Article 21 of the Constitution and it includes the right to enjoyment of pollution-free water and air for full enjoyment of life. If anything endangers or impairs that quality of life in derogation of laws, a citizen has right to have recourse to Article 32 of the Constitution for removing the pollution of water or air which may be detrimental to the quality of life.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">52.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">From the cases, cited above, it appears that right to life is not only limited to protection of life and limbs but also extends to the protection of health, enjoyment of pollution free water and air, bare necessaries of life, facilities for education, maternity benefit, maintenance and improvement of public health by creating and sustaining conditions congenial to good health and ensuring quality of life consistent to human dignity.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">53.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">If the right to life under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution means right to protection of health and normal longevity of an ordinary human being endangered by the use of tobacco and tobacco products then it cannot be said that fundamental right to life of a person has been threatened or endangered.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">54.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Article 18(1) of the Constitution says that the State shall regard the rising of level of nutrition and the improvement of public health as among its primary duties, and in particular shall adopt effective measures to prevent the consumption, except for medical purposes or for such other purposes as may be prescribed by law, of alcohol and other intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious to health. Though the aforesaid provision cannot be enforced by the Court it can be seen for interpreting the meaning of right of life under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution. A man has natural right to enjoyment of healthy life and longevity up to normal expectation of life of an ordinary human being. Enjoyment of healthy life and normal expectation of longevity is threatened by diseases, natural calamities and human actions. When a person is grievously hurt or injured by another his life and longevity are threatened. Similarly when a man smokes which is injurious to his health he suffers ailments and his life and normal expectation of longevity are threatened. It is the natural right of a man to live free from all man-made hazards of life and such right has been guaranteed under the aforesaid Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution subject to law of the land. No one has any right to endanger the life of the people which includes their health and normal longevity of an ordinary healthy person. Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution not only means protection of life and limbs necessary for full enjoyment of life but also includes amongst others protection of health and normal longevity of an ordinary human being. It is the obligation of the State to discourage smoking and consumption of tobacco materials and the improvement of public health by preventing advertisement of tobacco made products. Though the obligation under Article 18(1) of the Constitution cannot be enforced, State is bound to protect the health and longevity of the people living in the country as right to life guaranteed under Articles 31 and 32 of the Constitution includes protection of health and longevity of a man free from threats of man-made hazards. Right to life under the aforesaid Articles of the Constitution being fundamental right it can be enforced by this Court to remove any unjustified threat to health and longevity of the people as the same are included in the right to life.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">55.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The meaning of most commonly saying “health is wealth” is very simple and easy. It means our good health is the real wealth of our life which gives us good physique and mind and enables us to enjoy whole life by managing its all challenges. Good health promotes a good mental, physical and social health. The true face of a smoking is disease, death and horror-not the glamour and sophistication the pushers in tobacco industry try to portray.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">56.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Therefore, the High Court Division was perfectly justified in issuing directives to protect health and longevity of people because consumption of tobacco products is universally accepted to be harmful to health. When the right to life of the people is at stake, the legislature is under the obligation to enact law to protect such right as per directives of the Court. As such the question of encroaching upon the domain of the legislature by the Court does not arise.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">57.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In order to discourage smoking and usage of tobacco products Bangladesh has signed the Framework Convention on Tobacco Control (FCTC) on 16th June, 2003 and ratified the same on 10th May, 2004 in 56th Conference of World Health Organization.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">58.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the purpose of implementing the rules of the said Convention in Bangladesh, it was expedient and necessary to control smoking and production, usage, sale-purchase and advertisement of tobacco products. Therefore, Smoking and Tobacco Products Usage (Control) Act, 2005 (Act II of 2005) was enacted by the Parliament.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">59.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">When the impugned judgment was pronounced, the Tobacco Products Sale/Control Act,1988 (Act 45 of 1988) was in force. But the same law could not give the desired result as most of the consumers of tobacco were illiterate and they were not aware of the fundamental affect of consuming tobacco based product. Government being aware of this situation promulgated Ordinance No.16 of 1990 but unfortunately that Ordinance was not placed before the Parliament and ultimately it died a natural death. 60. Subsequently, the Parliament has passed the Smoking and Tobacco Product Usage (Control) Act, 2005 (Act No.11 of 2005 which was amended by the <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Smoking and Tobacco Usage (Control) (Amendment</span> Act, 2013). In addition, Government also framed the Smoking of Tobacco Product Usage (Control) Rules, 2006 under the Act of 2005. A revolutionary change has been made in respect <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">of prohibition on advertisement of tobacco product</span> <span style="color: red;">and on prohibition of smoking in public place and public transport by the Act of 2005 as amended till 2013 and the R</span>ules made thereunder. Directive D, E and F of the impugned judgment were implemented in full and directive No. C was implemented in part.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">60.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 5 of the Act provides for prohibition on advertisement of tobacco product, which provides as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“5. </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">prohibition on advertisement and promotion and control of sponsorship of tobacco products</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">- </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(1) No person shall– </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(a) publish or cause to be published advertisement of tobacco products in any print or electronic media, books published in Bangladesh, leaflet, handbill, poster, printed paper, billboard or signboard or in any other way;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(b) give or propose to give any sample of tobacco products to the public, for the purpose of enticing to buy tobacco products, either free or at a reduced price.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(c) give or cause to be given any donation, prize, stipend or sponsorship of any program for the purpose of advertisement or promoting the usage of tobacco products;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(d) publish or cause to be published advertisement of tobacco or tobacco products in any cinema hall, print or electronic media or web page;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(e) broadcast, display or describe or cause to be broadcasted, displayed or described any scene of using any tobacco products in any cinema, drama, or documentary produced in Bangladesh or produced in abroad but available and broadcasted in Bangladesh through television, radio, internet, stage show or any other public media; However, if it becomes necessary for the sake of story of a cinema, the scene of using tobacco products may be displayed provided that written warning about the harmful effects of tobacco products shall be displayed on the screen, according to the rules;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(f) produce, sale or distribute or cause to be produced, sold or distributed the cover, packet or box which is similar to the cover, packet or box of a tobacco product;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(g) display tobacco products advertisements at the point of sales, in any way. Explanation- To fulfil the objective of sub-section (1), “advertisement of tobacco products” means conducting any kind of commercial programs for encouraging the direct or indirect usage of tobacco or tobacco products.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(2) Nothing of article (e) of subsection (1) shall be applicable for the anti-smoke health related educational campaigns.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(3) No person shall use or cause to be used the name, sign, trademark, or symbol of any producer of tobacco or tobacco product, or entice any other person to use these if they participate in any social development work under the Corporate Social Responsibility programs or bear its expenses;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 27pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(4) If any person contravenes the provisions of this section he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months or a fine which may extend to one lakh taka, or both and if he contravenes the provisions more than once, every time the amount of fine or punishment shall be doubled.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">61.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Therefore, having gone through section 5 of the Act we find that there is blanket prohibition of advertisement and promotion and control of sponsorship of tobacco product. Sub-section (4) of this section provide that he, who contravenes the provision of section shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months or a fine which may be one lakh taka or both and he, who contravenes the provision of this section more than once every time the amount of fine or punishment shall be doubled.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">62.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 4 of the Act provides for prohibition of smoking in public place and public transport. Sub-section (1) of section 4 provides that subject to the provision of section 7 no person shall smoke in any public place and public transport and that if any person smokes in contravention of the provision of sub-section (1) shall be punishable with fine not exceeding fifty taka.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">63.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sub-section (2) of section 4 provides that if any person smokes in contravention of the provision of sub-section (1), he shall be punishable with fine not exceeding three hundred take and the penalty shall be doubled for each subsequent violation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">64.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 8 of the Act provides that outside the area marked or designed as a smoking area under section 7, the owner, caretaker or controlling person or manager of every public place shall in one or more places in the said area and the owner, caretaker or controlling person or manager of the public transport shall in the concerned transport arrange to display a notice “Refrain from Smoking, it is a punishable offence” in Bangla and in English language.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">65.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Directive-C of the impugned judgment was implemented in section 10 of the Act. Section 10 runs as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“10. </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">pictorial warnings etc. about health and other harms on the body of packets of the tobaccoproducts-</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(1) Health<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>warnings shall be printed on top of both sides of the packet, cover, carton or box of tobacco products, covering at least 50% of the total area of each main display area or if the packets do not have two main sides in that case covering at least 50% of the main display area, with colored pictures and accompanying text, according to the act, about the harms caused by the use of tobacco products and these shall be printed in Bengali. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(2) The following warnings shall be printed on the packet, cover, carton or box of tobacco products, i.e.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(i) For smoked tobacco products:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(a) Smoking causes throat and lung cancer;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(b) Smoking causes respiratory problems;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(c) Smoking causes stroke;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(d) Smoking causes heart disease;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(e) Second-hand smoke causes harms to the fetus;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(f) Smoking causes harms to the fetus.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(ii) For smokeless tobacco products:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(a) Consumption of tobacco products causes mouth and throat cancer;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(b) Consumption of tobacco products causes harms to the fetus.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(iii) Any other warning prescribed by law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(3) All packets, covers, cartons and boxes sold in Bangladesh shall carry the statement: “Sales allowed only in Bangladesh” and no tobacco products may be sold in Bangladesh without this statement.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(4) Packets, cartons, boxes, or covers of tobacco products shall not use brand elements (such as: light, mild, low-tar, extra, ultra, etc.) to create false impression about its impact and risk on public health.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(5) The printing methods on the packets, cartons, boxes, or covers of tobacco products of pictorial warnings described in subsection (2) and the statements described in sub-section </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(3) shall be determined by law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(6) If any person contravenes the provisions of this section he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months or a fine which may extend to two lakh taka, or both and if he contravenes the provisions more than once, every time the amount of fine or punishment shall be doubled.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">66.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">According to sub-section (6) of section 10 if anybody contravenes the provisions of this section shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding six months or a fine which may extend to two lakh taka or both or if he contravenes the provisions more than once, every time fine or punishment shall be doubled.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">67.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">What we are observing daily is that the provisions of this Act and the Rules made thereunder are not being properly implemented particularly as regards prohibition of smoking in public places and selling of tobacco products to minors. We have also noticed that in public places, the facilities relating to smoking such as ashtrays, matches, lighters are kept. It has become necessary to save our posterity from the curse of tobacco addiction and to inform them about the Smoking and Tobacco Product Usage Control Act, 2005 as amended by the Smoking and Tobacco Usage (Control) Amended Act, 2013 and also the Rules made thereunder. Therefore, we are inclined to give four more directives in addition to the directives given by the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">I. The law enforcing agencies are directed to implement the provision of section 4 of the Act, which provides that no person shall smoke in any public place and public transport and that if any person smokes in contravention of sub-section (1) shall bepunishable with fine not exceeding three hundred taka and the penalty shall be doubled for each subsequent violation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">II. The law enforcing agencies are directed to ensure that no one can sell tobacco product to a minor as per sub-section (1) of section 6(a) and sub-section (2) thereof provided if any person contravenes the provision of sub-section (1) he shall be punishable with fine which may extend to five thousand taka and if a person contravenes the provisions more than once, every time the amount of fine shall be doubled.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">III. The owner, proprietor of a public place shall ensure that no person smokes in that place. Ashtrays, matches, lighters and other things designed to facilitate smoking are not to be provided in public place where smoking is prohibited altogether. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">IV. The Ministry of Education, the Ministry of Primary and Mass Education and the National Curriculum Textbook Board (NCTB) are directed to incorporate a chapter in the curriculum of schools and intermediate colleges about the adverse effect of smoking and also about the latest law in this regard.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">68.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">There is nothing on record to show that the Government has taken any measure to implement directives (a) and (b) of the impugned judgments. Directives (a) and (b) are reproduced again as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">“a) The government shall take steps phase by phase to stop production of tobacco leaves in tobacco growing Districts of Bangladesh, giving subsidy to the farmers, if possible and necessary to produce other agricultural products instead of tobacco and for rehabilitation of the tobacco workers engaged in tobacco production, if possible with alternative beneficial jobs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">b) The Government shall restrict issuance of license for setting up tobacco industry or Bidi factory and direct the existing tobacco and Bidi Companies to switch over to some other industry to prevent production of Cigarette, Bidi and other tobacco related products, specifying a reasonable period for the purpose.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">69.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Therefore the concerned authorities of the Government are directed to start implementing directives (a) and (b) of the judgment of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">70.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, both the civil appeals are dismissed with the directives and direction made in the body of the judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">71.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Let a copy of the judgment be communicated to the Secretary, Ministry of Education, the Secretary, Ministry of Primary and Mass Education and the Chairman, National Curriculum Textbook Board (NCTB) each for information and necessary action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__November__18(2)/Issue__NOVEMBER_%2018(2)__C.%20A.%20204-205%20of%2001__Syed%20Mahmud%20Hossain,%20J__AD___3_.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">CIVIL APEAL Nos.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> 204-205 of 2001</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated 07.02.2000 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos.1825 and 4521 of 1999)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
688	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Government of Bangladesh  Vs. Abdul Bari Shah and others, (Soumendra Sarker, J.)	 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 788 of 2010  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Abdul Hai, D.A.G. with  Mr. Md. Shahidul Islam Khan, A.A.G. ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh represented by the Deputy Commissioner, Meherpur </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Abdul Bari Shah and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Evidence Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Soumendra Sarker, J</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__November__18(2)/Issue%20__November__18(2)__C.%20R.%20788%20of%2010__Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J__6.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 272.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; text-align: center;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh represented by the Deputy Commissioner, Meherpur</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Defendant-Appellant-petitioner.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">       </span></span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Abdul Bari Shah and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -0.3pt; text-align: center;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Plaintiff-respondent-opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Evidence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><br/>Section 115</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Scrutinizing the series of the documentary evidences specially the rent receipts issued by the concerned <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Tahshilder,</em> I find that the Government accepted the plaintiffs<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and their predecessor as tenants under him and granted rent receipts after accepting rent from them, and in this context; the learned Advocate on behalf of the opposite parties rightly referred the decisions of this court reported in BCR 1988 179 and 17 BLD 249. Hence, under the ambit of Section 115 of the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Evidence Act, 1872 (I of 1872) the Government</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> is now estopped from challenging the tenancy of the plaintiffs who were accepted as tenants under them by granting rent receipts after acceptance of rent. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>. . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Defence of Pakistan Rules, 1965</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Rule 169</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">It has been proved by sufficient credible tangible evidence that prior to 1965 A.D. the property-in-dispute has been transferred by the admitted original owner of the suit property, and as such the property can not </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">be declared enemy property or vested property</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> under the Defence of Pakistan Rules, 1965. In absence of any Government notification published in any official gazette as to the nature of the property as enemy property<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>or vested property as alleged from the side of the Government, it cannot be held that the property, under the Purview of Defence Of Pakistan Rules, 1965 has become vested or non resident property or that it has been leased out in favour of any body.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Government of Bangladesh Vs. Paresh Chandra Gharami and others, 50 DLR (AD) 70; BCR 1988; 17 BLD 249 and Government of Bangladesh Vs. Md. Mizanur Rahman 5 CLR (AD) 51 ref. </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Abdul Hai, D.A.G. with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in -.3pt .0001pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Shahidul Islam Khan, A.A.G.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">           </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                   </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Sharafutullah , Advocate<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">    </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .For the opposite parties.</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Soumendra Sarker, J.</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The Rules issued calling upon the Opposite party No. 1 &amp;
